Current Affairs Commentary

The Dispute Between "Yes" and "No" 11

Obscure

The League of Nations and the Sino-Japanese dispute. The resolution of the Northeast being forcibly occupied. Since the September 18th Incident, it has never considered effective methods of restraint. We certainly acknowledge that the League of Nations is merely a moral sanctioning body, absolutely without the strength to restrain the military aggression of Japanese imperialism. Moreover, one or two major powers have intentions of siding with Japan, tacitly approving all the atrocities of the Japanese army in the Northeast. There is a special background. At the same time, our country is directly victimized. Apart from appealing to the League of Nations to uphold "justice" as a moral sanction, there is virtually no more forceful expression. Because of this, the League of Nations procrastinates and even a moral sanction is begrudged and not given. The reason why they repeatedly dispute and cannot decide what is right and wrong is simply because the "Far Eastern balance of power" has already been broken, and the distribution of interests among the powerful countries is not yet even. That Japan has already done as it pleased, developing its "continental policy" to its peak. Even if our country loudly proclaims resistance, it will not harm the slightest bit the Japanese militaristic aggression. If this continues, the international balance in the Far East will become increasingly fragmented, and the Chinese market will become increasingly deteriorated. How can this be pleasing to Britain and France? And the United States will probably find it even more difficult to sit idly by.

In order to maintain its face and to maintain the "balance of power in the Far East" among the powers, the League of Nations cannot but express something. Therefore, the League of Nations' nineteen-nation committee deliberated back and forth and then issued a letter of inquiry to Japan. Its main point was to inquire:

'Does Japan "or" does it "not" recognize its acknowledged independent state of "Manchuria" as a method of resolving (the Manchurian problem)?'

And asked Japan to give a clear "yes" or "no" answer. If it considers it yes, then the nineteen-nation committee will prepare to accept Japan's reservation and proceed with mediation under Article 15, Paragraph 3 of the Covenant. If it is "no," then it will prepare a report in accordance with Article 15, Paragraph 4 with appropriate recommendations. In the League of Nations, this move has indeed exhausted its ability to be gentle and peaceful. But Japan believes that if it answers "yes," it would be tantamount to slapping itself in the face, admitting to abolishing the puppet "Manchukuo" it had created single-handedly, and submitting to the joint management of the powers. It would have to forcibly divide some of the vested interests in "Manchuria" with Britain and France. Even the United States, which wants equal opportunities, would certainly have to share a piece of the pie. If it should answer "no," then the proceedings under Article 15, Paragraph 4, would be unavoidable. Japan would still be forced to submit to "recommendations" (joint management) and sacrifice its exclusive control over the Northeast. Therefore, whether it is "yes" or "no," Japan is in an unfavorable position. Thus, the military department was indignant, the government clamorous, and groups gathered to discuss countermeasures. They stubbornly adhered to their traditional aggressive claims, stubbornly recognizing the puppet "Manchukuo" as an accomplished fact. The powers must recognize it; otherwise, they would "not hesitate to withdraw from the League of Nations."

Japanese militarists and spokespersons for the military department, such as the "Diplomatic Times," have long expressed contemptuous views of the League of Nations, advocating an Asian Monroe Doctrine. Its domination of the Far East and forcible occupation of Manchuria are indeed undeniable facts. Therefore, our country, with its lost territory and sovereignty, cannot recover it with empty talk of right and wrong without "iron and blood." Diplomatic negotiations are merely a formality, merely a superficial activity to socialize with the international community. Japan's invasion of North China, seizing Jehol, and disturbing Tianjin and Beijing, whether it withdraws from the League of Nations or not, will adopt the same method. Let us cite the statement of the army authorities on February 9, openly advocating that invading Jehol is a matter "within Manchuria (the puppet state)." Zhang Xueliang should not send troops; sending troops would be considered provocation. But the Japanese army's dispatch to Jehol is a "necessary means to maintain public order." What is even more outrageous is that it calls its invasion "the exercise of sovereignty by Manchuria (the puppet state)." The conclusion once again attempts to cover up and deceive, saying that this kind of invasion is "not provoking war against China," and that "in the future, there is no intention to provoke war." This kind of argument both disregards our country's territorial sovereignty and what regard does it have for the League of Nations' empty talk of justice?

Then, whether Japan withdraws from the League of Nations or not, its relationship with the League of Nations only means the loss of Japan's membership fees. Other than that, there is no loss whatsoever. Or perhaps it can stimulate them to find some "justice" in the international community. In the opinion of this writer, if Japan does withdraw from the League of Nations, although we will have difficulty finding opportunities to argue with Japanese diplomatic representatives in the future, diplomatically: First, Japan will fall into international isolation in the future. Second, the League of Nations cannot restrain Japan's atrocities, but it strengthens its violent monopolization, or it may prompt Britain to reflect and no longer listen to Japan one-sidedly. Third, break the joint management situation. Fourth, form a new international balance of power. Fifth, strengthen Japan's own difficulties. Its foreign trade, although it may not be affected immediately, but the lives of the general public will inevitably be difficult to maintain. Sixth, since Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, Japan can ignore any criticism from the League of Nations. Although our country has lost a kind of diplomatic application, in the future, we will engage in hand-to-hand combat with Japan and fight the final actual battle with strength, no longer relying on others, but striving to save ourselves.

In short, Japan's aggression against China, whether it withdraws from the League of Nations or not, or whether the League of Nations exists or not, the fact that it cannot seek a solution through diplomatic negotiations is obvious. The lessons of one year and five months should be fully alert. Hereafter, we might as well put aside "justice" and see what the outcome of "wrestling" will be.

Enemy Troops Fiercely Attack Kailu 12

The Japanese-Puppet Allied Forces Launch a Major Offensive Against Our Cui Brigade's Defense Line. Fierce Fighting Still Ongoing Yesterday Morning. Japanese Planes Bomb Villages, Killing and Wounding Over 300 Civilians. Righteous Armies Under Feng, Liu, and Li Each Outflank the Enemy.

(Beiping) A telephone call from Chengde at 7:00 PM on the 10th reports that today, Japanese troops in the Kailu area launched a fierce offensive against our Cui Brigade's defense line. At the same time, planes dropped bombs on nearby villages, resulting in the unprecedented tragedy of over 350 civilian deaths and injuries. Currently, a portion of the Cui Brigade is moving westward, forming a large encirclement of the Japanese and puppet forces. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) The troops of the Northeast Righteous Army under Li Chunrun and the regiment of Zhu Kuiwu engaged in fierce fighting with the enemy for three days in the area of Xinbin, Xinxian, Nankou, and Qianheiniuqiao. Due to running out of ammunition and supplies, over 400 of their troops hid their weapons and dispersed in disguise. The remainder were disarmed and dismissed by the Japanese soldiers. The Japanese plenipotentiary ambassador to Manchuria, Mutō, personally took command and led four echelons of rebel troops, over a thousand Mongolian bandits, and over 500 Japanese soldiers in a general attack on Kailu from Tongliao at 9:00 AM yesterday morning. (Relayed dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) Yesterday afternoon, Japanese planes again flew over Kailu County and bombed the city, setting fire to the south gate, burning several civilian houses and businesses. The Japanese side is still continuously reinforcing its troops. Enemy planes were also discovered in Fuxin County, dropping bombs and bombarding the troops of the Righteous Army under Wang Yunping. Fuxin County is also reporting tight conditions. With the battle on the Tang Yi hot side beginning, Military Headquarters Chief of Staff Li Zanbing has been dispatched to Kailu to inspect the situation. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) Yesterday, when the Japanese troops attacked Kailu, the Righteous Army under Liu Zhendong launched a counterattack from Daodeyinggang, engaging in fierce fighting for several hours, killing dozens of Japanese and puppet soldiers. Over 500 rebel troops under Yu Zhishan attacked Fuxin from Xinlitun yesterday, engaging in a two-hour battle with the Righteous Army under Li Haiqing in Shiwa, and were repelled. The Japanese cavalry unit under Miyake, with over 400 men, moved from Suizhong to Lingyuan on the Rebian road yesterday, clashing with a unit of the Righteous Army near Baishizuizi. Jia Qiuyi, commander of the 6th echelon of the Righteous Army under Liu Zhendong, and twelve officers and soldiers destroyed the Nanxinkaihe railway bridge in Zhangwu after Lunar New Year's Eve, preventing traffic for two days and causing dozens of casualties among the puppet troops. This unit has repeatedly repelled enemy troops and is currently awaiting orders in a certain location. Yang Jie went to Tianjin on official business today. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) At 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon, the Japanese Kawada Brigade and four echelons of puppet Mongolian bandits, under the cover of artillery, using ten tanks and twelve armored vehicles, launched a fierce attack on our Kailu, with five planes assisting in the bombing. We bravely resisted. At the same time, the Righteous Armies under Feng Zhanhai, Liu Zhendong, and Li Haiqing each outflanked the enemy, engaging in extremely fierce fighting with the Japanese and puppet forces. The fighting has not stopped yet, with heavy casualties on both sides. Kailu is quite tense. The authorities telegraphed orders to the front to resist to the death and dispatched a certain unit from nearby to reinforce. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) At 1:00 AM this morning, fierce fighting was still ongoing in Kailu. Our Righteous Army's radio station has been bombed and destroyed by the Japanese army. Our army has a very strong force and there is no cause for concern. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) Cui, the Brigade Commander of the Kailu garrison, reported to Tang Yulin this afternoon that fierce fighting continues in Kailu. The Japanese army has used artillery to cover several charges by puppet police rebel troops, but all have been repelled by us. The Japanese army in Kailu includes a squadron of the Miyake Cavalry Regiment, a unit of the 6th Division with approximately a thousand men, a squadron of the Kawada Regiment, a heavy artillery regiment, and a squadron of the 49th Infantry Regiment. The Japanese Command for Attacking Jehol is located at Dahushan. It is reported that the Japanese Garrison Commander Uno Saji and the rebel Zhang Jinghui and Yu Zhishan are currently in Tongliao. The Japanese army is currently transporting a large number of troops from Jinzhou to Tongliao and continuously transferring reinforcements from Shenyang. The puppet Fengshan Railway is filled with troop trains. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) A telegram from Chengde states that the Japanese army's plan of attack is to have the 8th Division attack Jehol, and to change the 6th Division to attack Yuguan. The units belonging to the 8th Division, except for a small number of troops stationed at various stations between Suizhong and Yuguan, are gradually moving towards Tongliao. The number of people who have now arrived in the Rebian area has reached more than 7,000. On the 10th, they began to pounce on our defense lines, and under the cover of planes and armored vehicles, the cavalry and infantry advanced fiercely in three routes. Our army's Cui Xingwu Brigade and the righteous armies of Li Haiqing and Liu Zhendong and others calmly dealt with the situation. More than a dozen enemy planes dropped bombs on Kailu City, causing great losses to merchants and civilians. Each unit of our army has established contact in the west of Kailu. That area is a vast desert, which will be disadvantageous to the enemy's armored vehicles. A regiment of enemy infantry blockaded Chaoyang yesterday. On the 10th, eight Japanese planes circled over Chaoyang for a week and left. In the afternoon, another Japanese plane arrived in Beipiao and transferred to Chaoyang for reconnaissance, and went east for about half an hour. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) At 8:00 AM yesterday morning, six Japanese planes flew from Tongliao to bomb Kailu Guojadian Nafen and other places, dropping bombs weighing 300 pounds, causing extremely cruel bombing. Fires broke out everywhere, and merchants and civilians were killed and injured, which was unbearable to watch. At the same time, the Japanese army attacked from Mangniuxiao, and others attacked Kailu from Chagoumen, led by Japanese with more than 3,000 Mongolian bandits. Our Kailu defense line was guarded by the Righteous Army under Feng Zhanhai. The two sides fought fiercely for ten hours. Our army is fighting with flesh and blood because the enemy's tanks and artillery are sharp. It is now calmly fighting. Our Kailu army is in a difficult situation. The Righteous Armies from various places have gone to support. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) Recently, the Japanese side has sent people to meet with traitors to spread rumors in Chenguantun, Liulongtai in the eastern part of Chaoyang, and Paozi Erdaogou and other places in Fuxin County to lure ignorant people and threaten local wealthy households to hang Japanese flags and force them to buy Japanese flags, each asking for 15 yuan. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) The Japanese troops attacking Jehol have been transferred since the first day. It is estimated that the 6th and 8th Divisions are stationed in the Jinzhou Sui and Tongliao area, the 7th Division is stationed in Asahikawa, the 14th Brigade and a part of the 9th Division stationed in Kanazawa have been mobilized one after another, and the rear reserve teams are the 19th and 20th Divisions. The 20th Brigade is stationed in Pyongyang, and the 39th Brigade was mobilized on the 4th of this month. It is scheduled to attack Jehol from Datong Jinzhao at the end of February. More than 500 Japanese cavalry arrived in Tongliao yesterday, seized more than 30 large carts, and moved to the north of Tongliao. The Japanese troops in Yuliangpu are in a westward trend. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Zheng Guilin Leads Troops to Attack Xingcheng 13

A Small Conflict in Shahe the Day Before Yesterday

(Beiping) Zheng Guilin led 5,000 people to attack Xingcheng yesterday. The vanguard troops engaged in fierce fighting with the enemy. Zheng commanded in Lishugoumen. From Xintai to Suizhong Zhaojiatun, the 240-li area, except for towns, is Zheng's defense area. A force of 12,000 troops has been assembled, and the momentum is huge. Nishankou is guarded by a neighboring unit. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) Outside Jioumenkou, the enemy cavalry attacked our Righteous Army at Lijiapu Songshuzui yesterday night. There was fierce fighting at the time, and the struggle continued until 2:00 AM this morning. There was also a small conflict in Shahe yesterday. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) The Shihe front line is becoming more and more tense. Three columns of Japanese armored vehicles are all firing up at the Yuguan station, waiting to be dispatched. The Japanese army is trying to repair the Shihe Railway Bridge, but our army is closely monitoring it on the west bank, and the enemy cannot succeed. Residents of Yuguan, hearing that the Japanese army will attack Ledu, have moved to the south coast behind the British and French barracks to take refuge. Yucheng has been under martial law since 4:00 PM. The Japanese army is inspecting residents very strictly, and the situation is tense. The Japanese garrison commander Wakakawa went to Suizhong by special train at 6:00 AM yesterday morning to hold a military meeting with officers of the 8th and 7th Divisions stationed there. He returned to Yuguan by special train at 5:00 PM. A unit of the 7th Division stationed in Desolate Land, about 500 people, advanced to Wanjiatun. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Song Ziwen Flies to Beiping to Negotiate North China Finance 14

(Nanjing) Song Ziwen flew to Ping at 9:00 AM on the 11th with his secretary Huang Chun Tao, Zhang Xueliang's secretary Li Shouqing, consultant Donner, and adjutant Zhang Hongcheng in a Ford plane to meet Zhang to discuss North China finance and inspect the Palace Museum and the work of moving northern cultural relics south. It is planned to return to Beijing by the original plane on the 13th. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) Song Ziwen came north from Shanghai by Ford plane at 9:00 AM yesterday morning to contact Zhang Xueliang about financial issues. Pingfang received the report before noon. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, welcomers went to the Qinghe Airport, including Wang Shuchang, Liu Chongjie, Wang Chengchuan, Tang Guozhen, and Hu Ruoyu, and more than ten people. At 3:10, the Ford plane flew to Qinghe and landed. Liu Ruiheng, Song's secretary Zhou Xiangxian, consultant Donner, and Zhang's secretary Li Yingchao came with Song. After Song got off the plane, he shook hands with the welcomers. Zhang originally planned to go to Qinghe to greet him, but he didn't go because of temporary matters. Song and Hu Ruoyu took a car to Shuncheng Wangfu to meet Zhang. Song told people at the airport that he would stay in Ping for two days before returning to Beijing. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Zhang Qun Prepares to Enter Sichuan 15

(Nanjing) Zhang Qun will go to Sichuan in the near future. Those who will accompany Zhang to Sichuan to assist in organizing the aftermath include Tang Xifen from the Ministry of Education, Yin Zusheng from the General Staff Headquarters, and Liu Gongqian from the Mongolian and Tibetan Association. Other departments are also selecting people. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Zhang Ji Receives North China Representatives and Listens to Party and Government Reports 16

(Nanjing) After the resolution to establish the North China Temporary Office of the Central Executive Committee, Chairman Zhang Ji has been receiving representatives from party departments in the north to listen to reports on the party and government situation in North China. A meeting of the various committees will be convened soon to discuss the organizational law and determine funding, etc. In about two weeks, the committees can go to Xinxiang to formally establish the office. All staff will be transferred from party departments in North China. After the office is established, the committees must go to various party departments to inspect and urge them to promote their work. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Red Bandits Roam the Guangze Area 17

Pursuit Troops Advance Towards the Fujian Border

The Fujian Pacification Headquarters Dispatches a Large Battalion to Encircle and Suppress

(Nanchang) A telegram from Fujian states that 3,000 to 4,000 bandits have arrived in Guangze and other places. Scattered bandits are continuously on the way from Lichuan to Shangguan. Pursuit troops from Zixi Lichuan are advancing towards the Fujian border. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Nanchang) The Fuzhou communities' welcoming Chiang Kai-shek association telegraphed yesterday to welcome Chiang and urged him to come to Fuzhou to supervise the suppression of bandits. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Nanchang) A message from Fuzhou states that there is no trace of bandits in Jinxi, and bandits have also withdrawn from Zixi. Zhu Mao's main force is gathering in northern Fujian. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Nanchang) A message from Wanzai states that the 16th Army, the 79th and 2nd and 3rd Independent Regiments of the Guard, are drifting in the area of Xiuwu, Tong, Wanzai, Chongyang, and Xian. The puppet 3rd Division is hiding in Dagang. The Yue Sen Division and the Li Regiment are joining forces with the Zhang Brigade to suppress the bandits. The bandits retreat to Buxia without making contact. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Nanchang) Zhang Nanxian, based on his experience in the three provinces, has formulated various items for Jiangxi's clean-up, aftermath, group defense, and self-defense for Jiang to adopt. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Nanchang) There have been no major operations in southern Jiangxi since Yu Hanmou returned to Guangdong. There are only a few puppet independent divisions, student supplementary divisions, and guard divisions in the central district of Yudu, Xingguo, and Ruijin. The main force of the Red Army has all fled with Zhu Mao to the Jiangxi-Fujian border. Those of the Central Army in Jiangxi are more than enough to suppress bandits, but the key to completely eliminating the Red bandits lies in Guangdong and Guangxi. A reporter recently inquired about the matter of the Central Government appointing Chen Jitang as the deputy commander for bandit suppression in Guangdong and Guangxi from the representative of the Eighth Route Army stationed in Jiangxi, and the representative replied that he did not know. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Fuzhou) After Guangze was captured by bandits again, the Pacification Headquarters decided to encircle and suppress them with a large army within a few days. It has ordered the entire Gui Zhenyuan Brigade to concentrate, and the Gui Brigade has been ordered to follow the order. The Brigade Headquarters also moved yesterday. Shun Chang was taken over by the Yun Brigade of the 38th Division. The Brigade also arrived in the area yesterday. Liu Zhennian also sent a team to assist in the suppression. A general attack will be launched within days. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Detailed Rules of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement Resubmitted for Revision 18

(Nanjing) The Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement is about to expire. All sectors of the country are angry at Japan's aggression against China. Although declarations have been made repeatedly to call for a halt, the Ministry of Finance believes that since diplomatic relations have not been severed, it plans to resubmit all the reciprocal detailed rules for revision. It has ordered the customs office to start preparations, collect materials, and draft the initial draft. Furthermore, the Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan has discussed the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement and will submit suggestions to the Central Political Council for reference. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Initiating Internal Reorganization of National Police Administration 19

(Nanjing) The Ministry of the Interior is reorganizing the national police administration. In addition to the police academies stepping up the training of basic talent, they are planning a comprehensive plan for reforming the system, strengthening forces, and raising funds. Regarding the standardization of names, all will be changed to the word "police" to avoid discrepancies. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Matters to be Undertaken by the Ministry of Finance Before Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan 20

(Nanjing) Regarding the abolition of taels and the change to yuan, the Ministry of Finance has tentatively set a trial run on March 1, and the mint will also start minting new coins at the same time. The plan is to implement it on July 1 of this year, when the annual general closing of silver and money industries occurs. During this transitional period, the Ministry of Finance will undertake: (1) The conversion of silver dollars and silver taels has been stipulated at a public price of 7 mace, 1 candareen, and 5 li per yuan, and exchanges in various places will also be implemented at this rate. (2) In the past, the exchange rate and the value of goods in silver dollars varied from province to province, and the names were different, which was detrimental to the monetary system. The National Government will issue an order to prohibit this. (3) The Ministry of Finance will formulate implementation measures for the abolition of taels and the change to yuan during the trial, and submit them to the government for promulgation and implementation. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Location for Preserving Southern Transported Antiquities Undecided 21

(Nanjing) The central government is still planning the location for preserving southern transported antiquities. It is rumored that it plans to find a suitable location in the Central Plains to properly preserve them. Rumors that they will be transported to Shanghai seem to have become a thing of the past. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Beiping) The second batch of more than 900 boxes of antiquities has been packed and is waiting for the train to depart. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Concern Over Yellow River Ice Thaw 22

(Nanjing) Today, a telegram from Jinan to this location stated that due to the melting of ice floes, the water level of the Yellow River in Shandong has risen sharply. At several places, the water is only one foot below the bank, and there is a risk of flooding and washing away. The authorities are now making every effort to protect it. (Reuters telegram on the 11th)

Control Yuan Decides to File a Second Impeachment Against Gu Zhutong 23

Names Listed Reach Two-Thirds of the Entire Body

(Nanjing) The Control Yuan will file a second impeachment against Gu Zhutong for the Liu Yusheng shooting case. This time, the number of Control Committee members who have listed their names for impeachment has reached more than two-thirds of the entire body. The impeachment documents will be submitted to the President of the Yuan for review and approval next week, and then submitted to the Central Political Council for referral to the Public Officials Disciplinary Committee for handling. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Bengbu) The Bengbu Journalists Association held a meeting on the 11th regarding Gu Zhutong's illegal shooting of Liu Yusheng and resolved to support the following: (1) Telegraphing the Central Government to revoke the punishment of Gu Zhutong. (2) Telegraphing the Control Yuan to continue to impeach Gu and refer him for disciplinary action. (3) Telegraphing the Human Rights Protection Association to provide strong assistance. (4) Telegraphing the Shanghai Journalists Association to argue reasonably and be willing to be a backing. (5) Telegraphing Gu to take the blame and resign to apologize to the people of the country. (6) Telegraphing the National Journalists Association to criticize Gu unanimously. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Administrative Regulations Reorganization Committee to be Established Soon 24

(Nanjing) Dai Chuanxian, Chairman of the Administrative Regulations Reorganization Committee, has summoned the committee members in Beijing for talks to exchange views. It is proposed to appoint Chen Daqi as the Secretary-General, and to invite renowned legal experts from various countries as consultants, as well as select law professors from domestic universities and members of the Legislative Yuan's Legal System Committee as specialist members. Once preparations are in place, the establishment will be announced. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Ministry of Finance Convenes Land Tax Conference 25

(Nanjing) At 2:00 PM on the 11th, the Ministry of Finance convened a land tax conference with the participation of the military, political, educational, industrial, and internal affairs departments, which was presided over by Yuan Lizhen, Director of the Tax Bureau of the Ministry. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance's Land Tax Reorganization Conference on the 11th has decided on measures, which are summarized into three main points: (1) The fixed amount of land tax surcharges shall not exceed 1% of the land price, and shall not exceed the above principle before the national land law price is determined. (2) The reduction and exemption shall be completed within the 22nd year of the Republic, and shall not be extended for any reason. (3) The principle of gradual reduction and exemption shall be based on the urgency of the use: first, reduce and exempt administrative fee surcharges; second, reduce and exempt business fee surcharges; and third, reduce and exempt education surcharges last. The Ministry of Finance is responsible for organizing the above-mentioned measures. After the organization is completed, it will be sent to various agencies for comments, and then submitted to the Executive Yuan for promulgation and implementation. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

The Appointment of County Magistrates Should Follow Legal Procedures 26

The Interior Ministry Informs Various Provincial Governments

(Nanjing) The Ministry of the Interior informs various provincial governments and requests them to forward the information to their respective civil affairs departments. In the future, the appointment of county magistrates should follow legal procedures, and resumes and credentials should be collected and sent to the Ministry for review and recommendation. County magistrates who have been formally appointed after passing the review cannot be replaced without reason, and military personnel are strictly prohibited from indiscriminately recommending county magistrates. (Special dispatch on the 11th)

Shandong Province's Entire Committee Decides to Conduct Inspections in Five Phases 27

(Jinan) Han Fuqu and the entire committee of the provincial government, directors of departments, and the president of the High Court decided to depart in five phases to inspect the entire province. Han will be in one phase and will depart first within days. The others will be in phases of two people. They decided to ride horses instead of taking cars to make it easier to chat with the common people. Japan Increases Troops in Northeast China 67

Many New Recruits Lack Experience

Sent to Manchuria for Special Training

Reuters Tokyo Dispatch, The Japanese newspapers have been reporting the dispatch of large numbers of troops to Manchuria for several days. Some of the troops have undergone some training in the barracks, but most are young new recruits who only enlisted on January 20. Normally, new recruits being transferred to Manchuria must complete their initial training in their designated military district before being transferred abroad. However, this is not the case now. Therefore, the Manchurian 　隊 [corps] is not as strong in manpower as the Japanese army. Among the new recruits being transferred to Manchuria, there are not many experienced officers going with them, because experienced officers must stay in Japan to train training teams and assign them to new recruit teams. In the Manchurian divisions, the number of people per division is only about 5,000 or 5,500, while the divisions stationed in Japan usually have about 8,500 people per division. This year's decision to transfer new recruits to Manchuria for local training, without initial training, will increase the number of troops in Manchuria from 40,000 to 55,000, or even more. These new recruits will naturally not be of much use in the first few months, but the training corps that go with them can serve as a rear support team in the event of war. The Japanese authorities are dispatching new recruits to Manchuria for local training, in addition to increasing the military strength in Manchuria, and it is said that there are two other purposes. One is to gradually acclimate new recruits to the climate of Manchuria, so that they will not be affected by the climate during wartime, and the other is to train new recruits in field warfare, because the work required in Manchuria is similar in nature to police work, which is completely different from what is usually trained in Japan. At the beginning of the Manchurian Incident, the combat power of the troops dispatched by Japan was not as effective as the six railway protection regiments, because the railway protection troops had been stationed in Manchuria for a long time and had received special training. The Japanese authorities believe that order in Manchuria may not be restored for several years, so they have decided that new recruits serving in Manchuria will henceforth be directly sent to Manchuria so that they can receive special training from the beginning, as the railway protection troops have received.

Japanese National Foundation Day 68

Mass Rallies in Tokyo and Osaka

Demonstrating the Aggressive Doctrine of the Former Emperor

Dent Agency Tokyo Dispatch, The National Foundation Day for the 2,593rd year of the founding of the nation began at 10:00 am. More than 100,000 citizens including Tokyo men's and women's youth groups, veterans, male and female students, various ideological groups, and groups from various Buddhist and Shinto sects participated. They all wore uniforms and hats, gathered in Ueno Park, Yasukuni Shrine, Shiba Toshogu, Meiji Jingu Gaien, Sumida Park, Fukagawa Park, Cotton Yarn Park and other venues, sang the military song Dai no Uta, and took an oath led by the master of ceremonies, vowing to sincerely embody the great spirit of Emperor Jinmu's founding of the nation and safeguard the imperial foundation. They then organized and went to Nijubashi Bridge, sang Banzai three times, and then returned to the venue to disband.

Dent Agency Tokyo Dispatch, Today is the memorial day of the 2,593rd anniversary of the founding of Japan. The Emperor personally attended a solemn ceremony at the Imperial Sanctuary and the Three Palace Sanctuaries, and held a grand banquet for internal and external officials in the Toyomei Hall. 群臣 [All the officials] were represented by Prime Minister 　藤 [Saito], and foreign envoys were represented by Soviet Ambassador Troianovsky, who delivered answering speeches. The banquet ended at one o'clock. From one o'clock to three o'clock in the afternoon, nobles, civil and military officials, members of both houses of parliament, and abbots of Buddhist temples paid homage to the Imperial Sanctuary. From five o'clock in the afternoon, the Emperor 出御 [made an appearance] at the Imperial Sanctuary Kagurasha and held the 御神學 [Imperial Divine Studies] ceremony.

Chinese United Press Osaka Dispatch, Today is the memorial day of the Emperor Jinmu, the first emperor of Japan, conquering and occupying Yamato Province. The Japanese government uses this day as the National Foundation Day to hold various memorial ceremonies and promote militarism. The city of Osaka, under the leadership of Osaka Prefecture, held a ceremony at Nakanoshima Park at 2:11 pm. All male and female teachers and students above middle school, students of the youth military training institute, youth groups, boy scouts, educational groups, women's associations, virgin associations, and civic-minded citizens, totaling 40,000 people, were mobilized. Each participating group was ordered to make two white flags, one for "宣掦國威 [promoting national prestige]" and the other for "發揮建國精神 [demonstrating the spirit of national founding]" (that is, demonstrating Emperor Jinmu's aggressive doctrine). They entered the venue holding the flags, performed the ceremony, and paid remote respects to the national flag, the Imperial Palace, the Imperial Ancestral Temple, and the Jinmu Temple (　原神宮 [Kashiwara Jingu]). Lieutenant General Kwon Do stood up and read the foreign declaration and the oath. Afterwards, they sang Banzai three times, and then dispersed into teams to parade through the important districts of Osaka. After the meeting, at 6:00 pm, a patriotic speech and a student patriotic speech contest were held at the Osaka Public Hall. Former Superintendent General of the Metropolitan Police Department Maruyama also came to Osaka to participate.

French Parliament Begins Debating Budget 69

Chamber of Commerce Decides to Strike to Protest

Havas Paris Dispatch, The House of Representatives began a major debate on the government's financial bill at 9:35 am. Danting, the leader of the right-wing party, raised a preliminary question, saying that the estimated budget deficit varies for each previous Minister of Finance, and the current government's proposal will definitely not be able to make up for it in full. Mr. Danting advocated for more austerity, and reduced the burden on taxpayers, and proposed issuing national lotteries, in order to preserve the vested rights of veterans. The government and the Finance Committee expressed their opposition to the above preliminary question, and it was rejected by a show of hands. Congressman Malan, a right-wing politician, continued to speak, reiterating Danting's criticism, advocating for tighter national spending, and effectively streamlining finances. As for reducing national defense spending, it is a criminal act at the moment. Congressman Digro, another right-wing politician, wanted to postpone the discussion of the bill, and the government and the Finance Committee came out in opposition and it was rejected by a show of hands. The general rapporteur of the Finance Committee, Ruzier, went on stage to explain the financial bill, saying that it could reduce expenditures by 217.3 million francs. Combined with the austerity bills passed previously, it could save a total of 574 million francs. As for the consolidation of tax revenue, it is estimated that it could increase revenue by 15,770,000 francs. Combined with the previously passed numbers, the total number of new revenues is 203.33 million francs. If the results of the exchange of public bonds are included, it can reduce the deficit by more than one million million francs. Ruzier also said that, according to the figures estimated by experts, it can be determined that the budget deficit will not exceed one hundred and five million million francs, and we can even hope that it will not reach this number. Ruzier further stated that the government and the Finance Committee expressed opposition to a complete balance between income and expenditure, because the exact amount of the deficit could not be determined. In conclusion, Ruzier declared that the argument against excessive spending was not fair, and that the public, in excessive pessimism, should have something to prevent it.

Reuters Paris Dispatch, The Chamber of Commerce and Industry, dissatisfied with the government's tax proposals, held a meeting of the chairmen of various organizations today and decided that on February 16, from noon to 7:00 pm, all stores nationwide would be closed to express their protest. However, employees involved in the 7 hours of the strike will be paid as usual. According to the new government's financial proposals, although only clerical staff will bear a very light tax, and veterans will even be 　免 [exempted], it is still subject to strong opposition. The Civil Servants' Union has unanimously rejected it, stating that it will never make the slightest sacrifice.

Germany Suffers Great Hardship

Gas Plant and Oil Refinery Explosion in Saar Region Kills Hundreds and Injures Over a Thousand 70

Schoolchildren Encounter Disaster on Way Home, Unable to Escape, One Tram Car Completely Destroyed and Missing

National News Agency, Saarbrücken, Germany, 10th A major change occurred in the town of Neunkirchen in the Saar region today, which is an unprecedented industrial disaster in Germany. The gas plant and the nearby Benzinol refinery suddenly exploded, causing the houses to be shaken and collapse one after another. At the same time, red flames 　溢 [overflowed], and the nearby streets were turned to ashes. It was 6:00 pm, and the workers in the factory had not dispersed. Male and female workers from other factories had finished work and were returning home one after another. Schoolchildren had also finished their classes and were returning home. They suddenly encountered the disaster on the way and were unable to avoid it. Therefore, in addition to those who were crushed to death by collapsing houses, there were also many people who were burned to death by stray fires on the way. As of 10:00 pm tonight, there have been 200 bodies found. More than a thousand people were injured, of whom 200 were seriously injured and feared dead. The number of casualties in the remaining disaster area is still impossible to calculate at this time because excavation has not been completed, but the number of deaths and injuries will definitely not stop there. The gas plant in this city is the largest in the Saar region and is located in the center of Neunkirchen. The town has a population of 45,000. The gas capacity of the plant is 120,000 cubic meters. The large gas holder is 80 meters high and 45 meters in diameter. The Benzinol refinery exploded first, and the gas plant was affected and exploded as well. Nearby towns heard the tremors, and the people in the full sea area felt tremors again after being shaken, suspecting that it was the recurrence of the earthquake. In Neunkirchen, 50 houses near the factory site were turned to ashes. The fire brigade rushed to rescue, but 　能遏止其波　他廠 [was only able to contain the disaster from spreading to other factories]. However, the disaster was extremely serious. The hospital was full of injured people, and temporary first aid hospitals were immediately established in countless numbers. The most peculiar thing is that one tram car happened to be driving in front of the factory when the disaster occurred and was instantly destroyed, and its whereabouts are unknown. The roofs of the factory buildings flew half a mile away, and part of the railroad was also destroyed, forcing transportation to be temporarily suspended.

Corpses Flying and Falling on Streets 71

Reuter's, Cologne, 10th: Lauenkothen in the Saar region, a major mining town, experienced a sudden explosion in its largest gas storage facility tonight. The heavy iron lid was blown a mile and a half away. One hundred people are dead, and at least one thousand are injured, with concerns that one hundred of the injured may also die. The sound of the explosion was heard as far away as Mannheim, and the flames were visible from thirty miles away. The oil storage area of the factory also exploded, immediately catching fire. Fifty houses in nearby streets were completely burned to the ground. Corpses were flying, falling on the streets, and some dismembered limbs were stuck to the walls, a truly unbearable sight. Many houses in neighboring villages were also damaged, demonstrating the immense power of the explosion. The entire fire brigade rushed to the scene, vigorously fighting the fire to prevent it from spreading. Doctors and nurses also arrived at the scene, bravely transporting the injured to hospitals, and some were performing temporary surgeries on the spot. It is expected that there are still corpses buried in the rubble. After the explosion, telephone and telegraph communications were disrupted due to the shock, so the news of the disaster was not widely known until rescue teams arrived from neighboring villages. The police authorities are now planning to order residents in all parts of the town to evacuate, as the gas leak is extremely dangerous. Trains cannot enter the station because the tracks are covered with debris. The factory, which had the most modern equipment in the entire Saar region, has been destroyed in an instant. Its gas coke ovens and electric furnaces have all been blown up.

Reuter's, Cologne, 11th: The corpses and the dying being pulled from the rubble have incomplete limbs. Residents in the danger zone are still very frightened. Women and children are abandoning their homes and seeking refuge in schools and other public buildings. Police officers from across the region are rushing to the scene of the disaster in heavy trucks.

Death Toll Gradually Rises to Over Three Hundred 72

National News, Saarbrücken, 11th: The explosion at the gas plant in Neukothen is now burning overnight, as people search for those buried in the rubble. The death toll has gradually increased. According to the latest news, it has exceeded three hundred people. In addition, over three hundred people were on the verge of death in hospitals yesterday. All hospitals are full, so temporary wooden sheds have been built to accommodate the injured. The gas plant is now surrounded by police. The devastation of the entire town is heartbreaking. Authorities fear further explosions, so they have ordered nearby residents to evacuate as quickly as possible. According to eyewitnesses, the current state of the town is as if it has been bombarded for several hours. The cause of the disaster is still unknown. When the explosion occurred, it shook for about a hundred miles. Even seismographs in distant observatories showed signs of tremors. The amount of loss is still impossible to estimate.

Excavation Work Still in Progress 73

Reuter's, Cologne, 11th: It is now believed that last night's disaster in the town of Lauenkothen was caused by the explosion of a gasoline tank, which ignited the gas. Sixty corpses have now been pulled from the rubble, and it has been confirmed that houses collapsed like stacks of cardboard, resulting in the death of entire families. The number of seriously injured has increased to two hundred and fifty, and the number of slightly injured is about several hundred. Local hospitals are full, so many injured people have been transported to hospitals in neighboring villages for treatment. A coke oven and several houses are still burning, but there is no danger of further explosions. Excavation work is still in progress. It is expected that it will take several weeks to clear the rubble and debris from the streets and repair the electrical and telephone lines. After this disaster, hundreds of households have no work to do, putting the residents of the town in dire straits.

Roosevelt's Foreign Policy 74

To Maintain the Stimson Doctrine in the Far East; To Clear up the Situation Left by the Great War in Europe

(Havas News Agency, Washington, December 12th) The "Foreign Affairs Review" in the United States, its relationship with the Democratic Party, and its position in American diplomacy are well known to us. In January next year, the magazine will publish an article by Colonel House discussing America's future diplomacy. House was a close friend of former President Wilson and was deeply trusted. His words are naturally interesting.

House's article elucidates "The Spirit of the United States Under the New Presidency of Roosevelt." According to his view, after the new Democratic government takes power in March this year, its goal will be to settle the situation left by the European War, to restore the world's trust, to remove obstacles to international commerce, and to enable the leaders of various countries to focus their energy on achieving new and constructive plans.

Reasons for the Failure of the Republican Party's Policies 75

Previous Republican governments also wanted to achieve the same goals, but they failed to consider economic problems in a practical way, and ultimately achieved nothing. Moreover, they were limited by state boundaries and narrow perspectives, which caused these problems to be delayed until today, making it doubly difficult for the authorities. It is said that the policies of Presidents Harding, Coolidge, and Hoover were all influenced by the Republican Party's selfishness. The party harbored unrelenting resentment toward former President Wilson, so that even after the end of the European War, wartime thinking still existed. The economic recovery failed, the situation was unstable, and all kinds of chaos existed in the world. It is not an exaggeration to say that the blame for all of this lies with the three Republican presidents.

Roosevelt Will Change Course 76

Since the Republican Party has failed in this regard, the new President Roosevelt should take a different approach to deal with the current problems. Based on his research of Roosevelt's previous statements, House said that he firmly believes that once Roosevelt takes office, he will treat both his own people and foreign governments with the same fairness and the same determination. House also said that the new president was a member of President Wilson's cabinet and was deeply influenced by Wilson.

House reviewed one by one the problems that Roosevelt should solve after taking office, such as tariffs, war debts, security, disarmament, and the Far East problem.

First, the Tariff Problem 77

According to his view, the tariff problem has completely changed since the European War. The United States was originally a debtor nation, but it has now become a creditor nation. In the past, American commercial settlements were often favorable, but today, because the United States has become a wealthy country, and European countries, as creditors of the United States, have now become poor, it is only logical that American commercial settlements cannot but change accordingly. The best solution now is to increase imports as much as possible, but reducing export trade is the worst policy. All of this depends on the tariff policy. President Hoover's policy was to raise tariffs, but between 1922 and 1929, the number of American manufactured goods exported increased greatly. House said that America's customers borrowed dollars in the United States and bought American products locally, but these customers could not sell goods to the United States in equal quantities because they suffered from unsound financial development. This development increased bank lending through low-interest policies and allowed the United States to absorb a huge amount of foreign securities. We do not allow foreign countries to earn American dollars to repay their debts to the United States, but instead give American dollars to foreign countries to pay interest.

House believes that this is a mistake in American policy and advocates the following theory: The real tariff problem is to enable foreign countries to earn a substantial amount of American dollars to repay their debts and to enable foreign countries to consume American goods without having to borrow money. According to the loans that various countries have borrowed from the American people, the amount that should be repaid each year is about 1,200,000,000 American dollars. We should enable various countries to no longer borrow new debts and to be able to repay part of them with goods and cash separately. We should take into account the loans that the United States has made, and we should also protect American foreign commerce to prevent it from being unfairly squeezed. This is what should be taken into account when formulating tariff policies. The current tariff rates should be reduced appropriately, and some should be greatly reduced. I say this not to advocate a free trade system, nor to advocate using tariff revenue to meet budgetary needs. I hope that tariffs will not hinder commercial competition and can recover the loans that have been made. The tariff system implemented by the United States after the war has another drawback, which is that it has aroused retaliatory measures from various countries. The creditor countries are looking around blankly, with no solutions. The United States should show them a compass so that they can find a way out. The new President Roosevelt intends to convene an international conference to discuss the issue of tariff reduction. This can become an important event in history. The improvement of the tariff system may be discussed by this conference or by the World Economic Conference. In short, all countries in the world have the same need for tariff reduction and economic settlement.

Second, the War Debt Problem 78

Regarding the war debt problem, House said that he believes that after the new government takes office, it should strive to make war debts no longer an international problem. This matter should be resolved through negotiations between the United States and the debtor countries. I think that in the spring of next year, the debtor countries should invite the United States separately to hold meetings to resolve the war debt problem in an organized manner, without having to adopt various means of refusing payment or temporarily suspending the payment of due installments. Roosevelt has declared his support for this kind of meeting and said that tariffs must be lowered so that foreign goods can be easily imported, and then foreign countries can repay their debts. House repeatedly stated that the uncertainty of transfer is one of the reasons why the world's economic situation has been slow to return to normal. He also said that when Roosevelt spoke on February 2, 1922, he hoped that the war debt problem could be resolved through rapid compromise. Roosevelt had a thorough understanding of this problem, so he made this statement, which was not an empty discussion.

House went on to say that the Allied countries in the European War had a sincere desire at the Lausanne Conference to temporarily forget the war debt problem and made significant progress on the German compensation problem to seek a final solution. The reason for this was that the people of various countries were aware that the compensation problem, covering Europe, would eventually lead to disaster, so it was better to resolve it with pain. The American people should also use the same reason and the same method to work hard to resolve the war debt problem so that it will no longer be a point of international dispute.

Third, the Disarmament Problem 79

Regarding this problem, House said that if we sincerely advocate disarmament, we should take action so that various countries feel that their land and property are safe and secure, and then disarmament will follow. There is no other way.

House then stated the plan of the Democratic Party's national convention, which advocates mutual consultation when treaties are threatened in order to maintain the Kellogg-Briand Pact in an effective way. House then stated that regarding the disarmament problem, political problems should precede technical problems so that various countries can engage in disarmament within a reasonable degree of safety. The more security that countries feel, the more their military power can be reduced to uselessness, and there is no one who would not be happy to reduce it.

For example, countries can jointly formulate plans to prevent aggression and mutually guarantee that no country can break this plan without prior warning or negotiation. Only with such guarantees can land disarmament be realized. However, if a country wants to retain its freedom to judge and act freely when an international group openly discusses whether a certain international action is consistent with its interests or whether it is beneficial to the maintenance of peace, or is unwilling to take any action with the attitude of an autonomous and responsible person, it cannot be equated with the same day.

Fourth, the Far East Problem 80

House said that in the Far East and Manchuria problem, the United States has two interests: one is to maintain the dignity of treaties, and the other is to maintain the traditional policy of open door. The principle announced by Secretary of State Stimson last summer was to have both parties restore the original situation through an automatic act or to resolve disputes through direct negotiations between the two parties under the guidance of the League of Nations. If the second method can be implemented, then the true purpose of the United States can be achieved, which is to maintain the Kellogg-Briand Pact.

Finally, House said that I dare to say that under the Roosevelt administration, American foreign policy will definitely tend to be generous and humane. We will not refuse the responsibilities that we should bear, but if the United States treats other countries fairly, we hope that other countries will also treat us fairly. We try to use fairness as the standard of action, but we sincerely hope that other countries will also treat all matters related to the happiness and security of the American people with the same principle.

Disarmament Conference Reaches Critical Juncture: German Representative Sharply Refutes Paul-Boncour 81

National News, Berlin, 10th: The General Committee of the Disarmament Conference continued to meet today. The German representative Nadolny spoke, refuting in detail the remarks made yesterday by French Foreign Minister Paul-Boncour regarding the right to equality. Nadolny said that the agreement of December 11 last year was the foundation for Germany's re-participation in the Disarmament Conference, so Germany could not tolerate any deviation from the agreement as long as it was in the conference. Nadolny also issued a solemn warning, saying that false and inappropriate disarmament conventions would not help the overall situation. Nadolny's remarks were endorsed by the German newspapers, which said that the debate in the main committee in recent days had clearly indicated that the Disarmament Conference had now reached a crossroads, and its success or failure would be determined in the next few days.

Britain Prepares Tensely for War Debt Negotiations 82

Lindsay Will Take British Plan Back to the US

Reuter's, London, 10th: The Cabinet Committee held its ninth meeting today to discuss war debts. The work of the committee is now extremely intense so that Ambassador Lindsay can go to the United States next Tuesday. Lindsay was also present at today's meeting. A special meeting will be convened on Sunday, at which a general discussion of the war debt problem will be held. After repeated discussions, Lindsay may be able to take back to the United States the British Cabinet's views on the war debt problem, the selection of the British delegation, and the organization. After Lindsay arrives in Washington, he will notify President-elect Roosevelt of the British Cabinet's views, and then Roosevelt will inform Britain and invite a delegation to the US to negotiate war debt issues. Before Lindsay meets with Roosevelt, the British government may not make any further statements. Lindsay may return to the US alone, without any advisors. Before the British delegation arrives in the US, Lindsay will be fully responsible for consulting with the US government.

French Aviator's World Record Competition Fails, Forced to Land Mid-flight by Headwinds 84

Reuter's, Gaza, Blanca, 10th: French famous aviators Bossoutrot and Rossi took off from Paris at 7:45 yesterday morning, planning to make a long-distance non-stop flight to the capital of Argentina in South America, breaking the record recently obtained by British aviators Gayford and Nicholetts. The attempt has failed. After flying over the Strait of Gibraltar at 5:20 yesterday afternoon, the two encountered headwinds blowing from Barcelona and landed here last night. This trip was intended to win a prize of 800,000 French francs from the French Ministry of Defense.

National News, Casablanca (Morocco), 10th: French aviators Bossoutrot and Rossi set off from Istres, France this morning, planning to go to the capital of Argentina in South America and seize the world long-distance non-stop flight record from British aviators Gayford and Nicholetts. Unfortunately, halfway through the flight, the engine overheated, and they landed here at 8:30 tonight. It is now believed that this failure was due to the rushed preparations.

Palace Museum Antiquities Depart Ping under Guard 85

Two Special Trains Departed South on the Morning of the 7th, Transporting 2,118 Boxes. A Second Batch Will Be Transported When the Executive Yuan Issues an Order.

Beijing Correspondence: The Palace Museum antiquities were transported from 8:00 on the evening of the 6th. The area from Tiananmen to the railway station was cleared, trams were suspended, pedestrians were cut off, and the guards along the way were strict. At 9:00, the transport began with heavy trucks and flatbed carts, passing through Wu Gate, Tiananmen, Zhonghua Gate, Zhengyang Gate, and finally to the Pinghan Railway Station. They were successively loaded onto the train on the ninth track platform. The first train contained archives and the catalog of the Siku Quanshu, and the second train contained the Siku Quanshu and valuable antiquities, a total of 2,118 boxes. The departure time was 7:00 on the morning of the 7th for the first train and 7:30 for the second train. It is expected that the special trains will arrive in Zhengzhou and then Xuzhou one after another on the morning of the 8th. The situation is recorded as follows:

Station Security 86

After the antiquities arrived at the station on the evening of the 6th, they were carried by the station porters, loaded into the train, and immediately sealed. Seals of the "Executive Yuan Antiquities Transport Supervisory Committee" and the "Palace Museum" were affixed. Station security was extremely strict. There were a battalion of the Military Commission's Beijing Branch Guard, a battalion of the Garrison Headquarters Guard, 130 military police, and about 200 policemen and the Fourth Security Team from the Public Security Bureau. Railway police were commanded by the General Section Chief and were responsible for duties inside the station. Because there were too many antiquities, they were transported in two trains. Director Yi Peiji and Supervisory Commissioners Li Shuhua and Weng Wenhao were all at the station to take care of everything. The first train consisted of twelve 40-ton iron boxcars, with the last car for the transport supervisors and military police. The second train consisted of thirteen cars, with the last car being a third-class passenger car and an official car, also for the transport supervisors and military police. The station only lifted security after the special trains departed.

Escorting Personnel 87

Fifteen people were selected by Director Yi Peiji to escort the antiquities on the train: Secretary Wu of the rank of Simplified Appointment, First-Class Staff Tang Zanxiang, Staff Yi Xianmo and Xing Zhiliang of the Antiquities Museum, Clerks Wu Zishi and Yang Zongrong, Staff Liang Yanwei of the Library, Clerk Qing Long, Clerk Wang Wenan, Staff Shi Kui of the Archives Museum, Clerk Zhang Guorui, Clerk Pan Tang, Section Member Yin Qiwen of the Secretariat, and Staff Xiang Jiajun and Liang Cai of the General Affairs Department. Liang Cai was in charge of general affairs and Xiang Jiajun was in charge of accounting. Each escorting personnel was given two days' meal expenses, with each clerk receiving three yuan per day and each staff member receiving four yuan per day. In addition, there were fifty guards from the Military Branch Garrison, sixty military police, and twenty Palace Museum guards, led by Bai Lang, traveling south to protect the antiquities.

Protection Along the Way 88

Before the antiquities special train departed, the Pinghan Railway Bureau received instructions from the Executive Yuan, ordering railway employees and police in various places to provide special protection for the antiquities. The original order stated: "The Executive Yuan orders that, according to Director Yi (Peiji) of the Beijing Palace Museum, the antiquities transported to the capital will be transported to the Pinghan Railway Station at 9:00 p.m. and depart at 7:00 a.m., etc. You are hereby ordered to separately instruct the employees and police of all sections of the Pinghan, Longhai, and Jinpu Railways to provide special and thorough protection. Please also report the details of the departure and the time of arrival at each station."

Number Transported South 89

The antiquities transported south this time are part of the archives, the Siku Quanshu, and the Antiquities Museum. The first batch transported included 1,064 boxes of documents and archives, 602 boxes of books (including 536 boxes of the Siku Quanshu, 32 boxes of the Tushu Jicheng, and 34 boxes of Ming and Qing palace editions, etc.), and 452 boxes of antiquities, totaling 2,118 boxes. There are still 900 boxes to be transported, which will be transported for the second time when the Executive Yuan issues an order to Ping. The total number of antiquities in the two batches that have been transported and are waiting to be transported is about 3,000 boxes, accounting for about one-tenth of all the items in the Palace Museum. The categories and quantities of antiquities are: 600 boxes from the Antiquities Museum, 300 boxes of archives, and over 1,000 boxes of the Siku Quanshu. Specifically, the categories include: Zi: Qing History archives, a total of 20 categories; Chou: Antiquities, I. 1,159 pieces of Qing porcelain from Chengqian Palace, II. 260 pieces of Shang and Zhou bronzes from Jingren Palace, III. Seven types of antiquities from eight exhibition rooms, including A. 701 pieces of Qianlong's personal collection of playthings, B. 39 pieces of various bonsai screens and other decorations from two locations, C. 51 whole elephant tusks presented by Qing dynasty tributaries, D. 67 various knives and swords used by Qing dynasty emperors and collected from various places, E. 352 various gold and jade utensils, F. 13 various old rubbings of inscriptions, G. 57 ancient mirrors from various dynasties, as well as 176 pieces of old jade, 164 pieces of new jade, and famous paintings from various dynasties and paintings by Castiglione, etc.; Yin: Books, I. 939 rare books, II. 559 palace editions, III. 990 classics, IV. 1,316 historical works, V. 1,539 philosophical works, VI. 1,845 collections of works, VII. 2,814 local chronicles, VIII. 1,559 books from the Guanhai Tang collection, IX. 362 Manchu and Mongolian documents. In addition, 5,319 copies of duplicate books and 1,175 boxes of miscellaneous books will be temporarily left in Ping.

Zhou Will Be Released 90

Zhou Zhaoxiang, a member of the Beijing Municipal Public Antiquities Association, was arrested a few days ago by the Ping Municipal Public Security Bureau pursuant to an order from the Executive Yuan, accusing him of colluding with a puppet state, and detained in the preferential treatment room of the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau. Subsequently, Xiong Xiling, Zhou Zuomin, Leng Jiaji, and others petitioned the Public Security Bureau for his release, but to no avail. Mayor Zhou Dawen said, "Mr. Zhou's arrest was pursuant to an order from the Executive Yuan, and the release procedure must also have an order from the Executive Yuan. I (the Mayor) have telegraphed the Executive Yuan for instructions today (the 7th), since the antiquities have been moved south, Mr. Zhou seems to be able to be released. However, I cannot predict when he will be released at this time. It must be handled after the Executive Yuan's reply telex arrives in Ping. In short, Mr. Zhou will be bailed out soon." (7th)

Japan Discovers a Major Judicial Official Fraud Case 91

"So-called Organized Nation," says Tokyo Jiji Shinpo: Recently, fraud cases have been discovered one after another with the sacred court as a background. Although the prosecuting authorities have increased the crackdown, in addition to the cases of the violent gangs, vicious lawyers, and prison officers in the Tokyo District Court Prison Department, now there are unscrupulous people using the names of high-ranking judicial officials to organize the Imperial Jury Association, soliciting 6,000 members and defrauding 20,000 to tens of thousands of yuan. Currently, in addition to arresting the fraudsters Araki and Fujita, the mastermind, and others, many people, including the chairman of the association's board of directors, the accounting director, and the secretary, have all fled. Supporting members were issued letters of thanks from the former Minister of Justice, and were taught knowledge of the jury law. As a result, more than 1,000 supporting members and 50 regular members were lured to join, and the membership fees obtained reached 20,000 to tens of thousands of yuan.

The income from compensation allows credit to be maintained, and business can flourish. Life insurance can also be used in joint ventures to prepare for shareholders unexpectedly withdrawing capital. Life insurance companies are, in fact, centralized financial institutions upon which various industries rely for development. ㈤ Promoting Social Peace 99

Life insurance has mutual benefits for individuals, families, education, and industry and commerce, so it goes without saying that it contributes to the tranquility of society. When the lives of the people are stable, the security of society will naturally be strengthened. ㈥ Enhancing National Health 100

Life insurance companies handle business with scientific methods as the guiding principle. When purchasing life insurance, a physical examination is required. Changes in physiology and symptoms of disease are often not noticed on a daily basis, but after an examination, one suddenly becomes aware. Therefore, people diligently pursue hygiene and correct weaknesses. If the entire nation competes to promote this, a healthy nation can be expected. Moreover, life insurance companies all engage in social work, using the remaining capacity of their business to promote public health and participate in various health movements, especially striving to research methods for preventing and eradicating disease.

Rapid Development of the Life Insurance Industry in Japan 101

Mr. Jones, the Vice President of New York Life Insurance Company, recently gave a speech at the Life Insurance Association Conference in New York, praising the development of the life insurance industry in Japan.

He said: "Fifty years ago, Japan had no life insurance, nor did it know what life insurance was. However, currently Japan ranks fourth in the world in terms of life insurance authority. The United States federal government is a giant in the world life insurance industry, accounting for 70% of the world's total business, followed by the United States, and then Canada.

"Japan is making extraordinary efforts in the development of the insurance industry. Its development period can be divided into three stages: 1880 was the beginning of the Japanese life insurance industry, after 1900 was the development period, and after 1916 was the most prosperous period.

"Many aspiring foreign students who come to the United States to study life insurance are almost all sent by Japan. They often visit and inspect the internal organization and business strategies of various companies for application when they return home.

"Insurance, including life and property insurance, is a required subject in the business departments of every university in Japan, and almost all senior commercial high schools have a course on the principles of insurance.

Why should every wealthy person in Japan buy life insurance?

There are several reasons why a wealthy person should buy life insurance:

㈠ To obtain readily available funds at the lowest cost, so that his property and business will not suffer losses.

㈡ To ensure that his descendants receive a fixed inheritance after his death.

㈢ To maintain his original social status after investment failures.

㈣ To ensure the safety of his property after death.

㈤ To provide security for other investment failures to avoid property loss.

㈥ To provide security for property loss in case of other business failures.

㈦ To ensure a fixed income in case of future business failures.

㈧ To avoid property loss.

㈨ To provide security for estate taxes.

㈩ The insured assets can be enjoyed and used after insurance, not just after twenty years.

㈩㈠ To obtain good and stable investments.

㈩㈡ To eliminate speculative ideas.

㈩㈢ To obtain a fixed income when one is old and unable to work.

㈩㈣ To provide economic security for the family.

"The staff of various insurance companies in Japan have been trained in the United States, and all business methods are based on the standards of our association. Therefore, their knowledge and experience have been improved, and their business can be developed.

"Currently, the world's attention to life insurance is focused on the United States, but our association's recent observations suggest that this situation may shift to other countries. The United States has realized this and is willing to use its successful experience in the insurance industry to help the development of the life insurance industry in other countries when the opportunity arises. At the same time, let us gradually reduce the record of world insurance coverage maintained by the United States, so that all countries can achieve balanced development in life insurance.

"The necessary conditions for developing the insurance industry in various countries in the world are to promote social evolution, improve living standards, and maintain world peace, and then smooth development can be achieved."

American President Discovers Double Case 102

The protagonist was originally an insurance manager. The president's joke made business boom.

Recently, an interesting double case occurred in the United States, which not only caused a sensation in society but also remains a beautiful story in the life insurance industry to this day. When Roosevelt was elected last year, newspapers everywhere competed to publish Luo's portrait so that those who admired him could catch a glimpse of his style. Unexpectedly, a man named Kennard, an insurance manager in Rochester, New York, looked exactly like Roosevelt, so much so that the local people, after discovering this, saw it as an honor to catch a glimpse of this fake president, and some even mistakenly thought it was Roosevelt himself. Therefore, Kennard was often surrounded by many people when he went out so they could catch a glimpse of his style, and the number of people who came to Kennard's residence every day to seek an audience was even more numerous. Later, Roosevelt learned of the news and personally went to Rochester to meet Kennard. Upon meeting, he was also astonished and blurted out, "This is my brother." After Kennard's reputation was enhanced a hundredfold, local people who purchased life insurance have since considered it an honor to be handled by this "president's brother." Not only did Kennard's business flourish, but the company also gained many new policyholders as a result, which shows the American people's admiration for Roosevelt.

Losing Sharpness Brings Unexpected Fortune 103

In Macanama, London, there was a person who specialized in long howls as his profession. To protect his sharp pronunciation, he insured his voice with an insurance company. It was stipulated at the time that if his voice was accidentally damaged, the company would pay him US$50 per week in compensation. Once, his sharp throat sound was accidentally damaged and he could not make long howling sounds. The company not only fulfilled the contract but also increased the compensation to US$150 per week and paid it until his throat sound recovered. At that time, he was very happy to hear this news, because although his throat sound was temporarily lost and he could not engage in his profession, the insurance compensation he could get every week was unexpectedly US$5 more than his previous salary. This is truly a blessing in disguise.
